id="sidebarContent"><p class="sidebar_navTopLabel__xl_5k">Contents</p><ol><li><a class="sidebar_link___4reK sidebar_linkActive__wuL2e" rel="noopener" href="#article">Article</a></li><li><a class="sidebar_link___4reK" rel="noopener" href="#more-blogs">More blogs</a></li></ol></div><div class="sidebar_copyUrlWrapper__n99w0  hidden lg:flex" style="border-bottom:none"><button type="button" class="sidebar_copyUrl__P5IEw">Copy URL</button></div><div class="sidebar_copyUrlWrapper__n99w0 flex lg:hidden" style="border-bottom:none;border-top:none"><button type="button" class="sidebar_copyUrl__P5IEw">Copy URL</button></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="hidden lg:block" style="margin-bottom:-0px"></div><div class="" id="article"><div class=""><div class="wysiwyg_module_root__WLg4d container"><div class="default-grid"><div class="col-span-full lg:col-span-8 lg:col-start-4"><div class="wysiwyg_module_content__XGnZp"><p>Infostealer is one of the most profitable tools for cybercriminals, as information gathered from systems infected with this malware could be sold in the cybercrime underground or used for credential stuffing attacks.В The Zscaler ThreatLabZ team came across a new Infostealer called PurpleWave, which is written in C++В and silently installs itself onto a userвҖҷs system. It connects to a command and control (C&amp;C) server to send system information and installs new malware onto the infected system.</p>

<p>The author of this malware is advertising and selling PurpleWave stealerВ on Russian cybercrime forums for 5,000 RUB (US$68) with lifetime updates and 4,000 RUB (US$54) with only two updates.<br/>
<br/>
<img alt="PurpleWave selling post on the Russian forum" data-entity-type="" data-entity-uuid="" src="https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/purple_website.JPG" loading="lazy" decoding="async"/></p>

<p><em>Figure 1: A PurpleWave selling post on a Russian forum.</em></p>

<p>The author selling PurpleWave claims that this stealer is capable of stealing passwords, cookies, cards, and autofill forms of ChromiumВ and Mozilla browsers. This stealer also collects files from the specified path, takes screenshots, and installs additional modules.</p>

<p>The capabilities of the PurpleWave stealer include:</p>

<ul>
	<li>StealingВ passwords, cookies, cards, autofill(s) data, browser history from Chromium and Mozilla.</li>
	<li>CollectingВ files from the specified path</li>
	<li>Capturing theВ screen</li>
	<li>StealingВ system information</li>
	<li>StealingВ Telegram session files</li>
	<li>StealingВ Steam application data</li>
	<li>StealingВ Electrum wallet data</li>
	<li>LoadingВ and executingВ additional module/malware</li>
</ul>

<p><img alt="PurpleWave Login Panel" data-entity-type="" data-entity-uuid="" src="https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/purple_panel.PNG" loading="lazy" decoding="async"/></p>

<p><em>Figure 2: The PurpleWave login panel.</em></p>

<p>The author also built a dashboard where the attacker can keep an eye on the infection counts according to dates, access the stolen logs of infected machines, and change the malware configuration settings.</p>

<p><img alt="PurpleWave Infection dashboard" data-entity-type="" data-entity-uuid="" src="https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/purple_panel1.jpg" loading="lazy" decoding="async"/></p>

<p><em>Figure 3: The PurpleWave infection dashboard.</em></p>

<p>The dashboard also provides the attacker with the ability to customize the configuration of the PurpleWave stealer.</p>

<p><img alt="Dashboard for customizing PurpleWave configuration" data-entity-type="" data-entity-uuid="" src="https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/purple_panel3.jpg" loading="lazy" decoding="async"/></p>

<p><em>Figure 4: The dashboard for customizing the PurpleWave configuration.</em></p>

<p>В </p>

<p><strong>Technical analysis</strong></p>

<p>Upon execution of the PurpleWave binary, it gives a fake error message in the Russian language that can be customized by the attacker in their panel. But in the background, it performs all of its malicious activities.</p>

<p><img alt="Fake error message (translated:Memory control blocks damaged)" data-entity-type="" data-entity-uuid="" src="https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/purple_fakeerror.PNG" loading="lazy" decoding="async"/></p>

<p><em>Figure 5: The fake error message in Russian. (It translates to: Memory control blocks damaged.)</em></p>

<p>The name of the stealer (PurpleWave) and the version (1.0) are hardcoded and encrypted in the binary. Most of the strings in the binary are encrypted, but they getВ decrypted on runtime with the help of the decryption loop present in the binary (shown in Figure 6).</p>

<p><img alt="Common Decryption function for encrypted strings in binary" data-entity-type="" data-entity-uuid="" src="https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/purple_decryptionloop.PNG" loading="lazy" decoding="async"/></p>

<p><em>Figure 6: The common decryption function for the encrypted strings in the binary.</em></p>

<p>The PurpleWave binary creates a mutex with the name вҖңMutexCantRepeatThisвҖқ to avoid multiple executions of malware instances. After that, it sends the HTTP POST request with the custom header and body to the C&amp;C URL to get the configuration data.</p>

<p><img alt="Sending request to get the config data" data-entity-type="" data-entity-uuid="" src="https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/purple_configolly.PNG" loading="lazy" decoding="async"/></p>

<p><em>Figure 7:В Sending request to the C&amp;C server to get the config data.</em></p>

<p>It creates an HTTP request header with content type as вҖңform-dataвҖқ. The boundary is assigned with вҖңboundaryaswellвҖқ to act as a marker and user agent is set with вҖңappвҖқ. It creates a request body with a form name as вҖңidвҖқ and the value assigned to it is 1.</p>

<p><img alt="Request with custom header and body to get the configuration" data-entity-type="" data-entity-uuid="" src="https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/wireshark_config.JPG" loading="lazy" decoding="async"/></p>

<p><em>Figure 8: The configuration request with the custom header and body.</em></p>

<p>The received data contains the customized configuration, which may change per the binary. We have observed three different configurations and different hosts of the PurpleWave binaries.</p>

<p><img alt="Configuration from different PurpleWave binaries" data-entity-type="" data-entity-uuid="" src="https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/config_comapre.png" loading="lazy" decoding="async"/></p>

<p><em>Figure 9: The configuration from different PurpleWave binaries.</em></p>

<p>dirs - It consists of directory information from which files to be collected.<br/>
fake - It has the fake alert message to be shown to the user on execution.<br/>
loaders - It consists of an additional module name to be installed on the infected system.</p>

<p>For Config-2, PurpleWave will traverse path вҖң%userprofile%/DesktopвҖқ and collect the files having extensions txt, doc and docx. In Config-3, it will not collect any files but it has a module named вҖңKv2TDW4OвҖқ in the loaders, which will get downloaded and executed on the system.<br/>
В </p>

<p><strong>Installing additional modules</strong></p>

<p>For installing additional modules mentioned in the received configuration (Config-3), PurpleWaveВ again creates an HTTP POST request with the same headers mentioned in the previous request to the C&amp;C host followed by вҖң/loader/module_nameвҖқ.</p>

<p><img alt="Request to download additional module" data-entity-type="" data-entity-uuid="" src="https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/wireshark_loader.JPG" loading="lazy" decoding="async"/></p>

<p><em>Figure 10: The request to download an additional module.</em></p>

<p>PurpleWave enumerates the loaders list from a JSON configuration, downloads the module name from the C&amp;C server and stores it in %appdata% directory, then executes it.</p>

<p><img alt="Downloading and executing additional modules" data-entity-type="" data-entity-uuid="" src="https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/purple_loader.PNG" loading="lazy" decoding="async"/></p>

<p><em>Figure 11:В Downloading and executing additional modules.</em></p>

<p>The downloaded module that we observed in some PurpleWave binary is the Electrum wallet stealer, which is written in .NETВ and capable of stealing Electrum wallet data from the infected system.</p>

<p><img alt="Collecting Electrum wallet data" data-entity-type="" data-entity-uuid="" src="https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/walletstealer.PNG" loading="lazy" decoding="async"/></p>

<p><em>Figure 12:В Collecting Electrum wallet data.</em></p>

<p>В </p>

<p><strong>Data stealing</strong></p>

<p>PurpleWaveВ is capable of stealing credentials, autofills data, card data, cookies, and browser history from Chromium and Mozilla.</p>

<p>For Chromium browsers, it fetches the login credentials from вҖң\%AppData%\Local\{Browser}\User Data\Default\Login DataвҖқ, cookies from вҖң\%AppData%\Local\{Browser}\User Data\Default\CookiesвҖқ,В and other information, such as autofills data, card data, and browser history, from вҖң\%AppData%\Local\{Browser}\User Data\Default\Web DataвҖқ.</p>

<p><img alt="Stealing BrowserвҖҷs data" data-entity-type="" data-entity-uuid="" src="https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/browser_data.png" loading="lazy" decoding="async"/></p>

<p><em>Figure 13:В Stealing browserВ data.</em></p>

<p>The stolen browser info is collected in the form of a form-data field with the names shown below followed by their value.<br/>
Username - browser[BrowserName][passwords][index][login]<br/>
Password - browser[BrowserName][passwords][index][password]<br/>
<img alt="Stolen Browser info" data-entity-type="" data-entity-uuid="" src="https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/browser_collected.png" loading="lazy" decoding="async"/></p>

<p><em>Figure 14:В Stolen browser information.</em></p>

<p>Along with the browserвҖҷs data, the stealer captures the current screen and appends it to the browser&#x27;s stolen data in the form-data with the filename as вҖңscreenshot.pngвҖқ.</p>

<p><img alt="Captured Screenshot" data-entity-type="" data-entity-uuid="" src="https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/screenshot.JPG" loading="lazy" decoding="async"/></p>

<p><em>Figure 15: A captured screenshot.</em></p>

<p>After that, it collects all the information about infected systems, such as operating system, CPU info, GPU info, machine GUID, username, machine name, and more.</p>

<p><img alt="Collected system info" data-entity-type="" data-entity-uuid="" src="https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/about_send.png" loading="lazy" decoding="async"/></p>

<p><em>Figure 16: TheВ system information collected by PurpleWave.</em></p>

<p>The stealer also collects the SSFN files from the Steam application. The Steam application is used for playing, discussing, and creating games. The SSFN file exists to verify the users each time they login to their Steam account. It fetches the Steam path from the registry вҖңSoftware\\Valve\\SteamвҖқ and reads all the SSFN files stored into the config directory.</p>

<p><br/>
PurpleWave also steals session-related files from the Telegram application. It reads the value of the default key in the system registry branch вҖңHKCU\Software\Classes\tdesktop.tg\DefaultIconвҖқВ to obtain a path of Telegram and collects all the files starts with вҖңmapвҖқ in the вҖңD877F783D5D3EF8CвҖқ directory.</p>

<p><br/>
<img alt="Collecting Steam data and Telegram data" data-entity-type="" data-entity-uuid="" src="https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/steam_telegram.png" loading="lazy" decoding="async"/></p>

<p><em>Figure 17:В Collecting Steam and Telegram data.</em></p>

<p>PurpleWave merges all the collectedВ fileВ data, browser data, screenshots, Steam data, Telegram data, and system info, then sends it to a C&amp;C server using an HTTP POST request.</p>

<p><img alt="Sending stolen data to C&amp;C server" data-entity-type="" data-entity-uuid="" src="https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/gate_post.JPG" loading="lazy" decoding="async"/></p>

<p><em>Figure 18:В Sending stolen data to C&amp;C server</em></p>

<p>В </p>

<p><strong>Coverage</strong></p>

<p>The observed indicators in this attack were successfully blocked by the Zscaler Cloud Sandbox.</p>

<p><img alt="The Zscaler Cloud Sandbox report for the PurpleWave Stealer" data-entity-type="" data-entity-uuid="" src="https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/sandbox1.JPG" loading="lazy" decoding="async"/></p>

<p><em>Figure 19:В The Zscaler Cloud Sandbox report for PurpleWave.</em></p>

<p>In addition to sandbox detections, ZscalerвҖҷs multilayered cloud security platform detects indicators at various levels. The following advanced threat protection signatures have been released for detecting the malware:<br/>
<a href="https://threatlibrary.zscaler.com/?keyword=Win32.PWS.PurpleWave">Win32.PWS.PurpleWave</a></p>

<p><strong>Conclusion</strong></p>

<p>Zscaler believes that PurpleWave represents an active and ongoing threat, as theВ C&amp;CВ servers are still alive and responding as of this writing.В The malware also still appears to be available for purchase on the black market. PurpleWave has incredible potential to steal sensitive information. The malware is in the early stages of development, with the author likely to enhance its stealing capabilities and add more features. We will continue to keep track of this threatВ to ensure coverage.</p>

<p><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/"><strong><u>MITRE ATT&amp;CK</u></strong></a><strong>в„ў tactic and technique mapping</strong></p>

attacks.В The Zscaler ThreatLabZ team came across a new Infostealer called PurpleWave, which is written in C++В and silently installs itself onto a userвҖҷs system. It connects to a command and control (C\u0026amp;C) server to send system information and installs new malware onto the infected system.\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003eThe author of this malware is advertising and selling PurpleWave stealerВ on Russian cybercrime forums for 5,000 RUB (US$68) with lifetime updates and 4,000 RUB (US$54) with only two updates.\u003cbr\u003e\r\n\u003cbr\u003e\r\n\u003cimg alt=\"PurpleWave selling post on the Russian forum\" data-entity-type=\"\" data-entity-uuid=\"\" src=\"https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/purple_website.JPG\" loading=\"lazy\" decoding=\"async\"\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cem\u003eFigure 1: A PurpleWave selling post on a Russian forum.\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003eThe author selling PurpleWave claims that this stealer is capable of stealing passwords, cookies, cards, and autofill forms of ChromiumВ and Mozilla browsers. This stealer also collects files from the specified path, takes screenshots, and installs additional modules.\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003eThe capabilities of the PurpleWave stealer (It translates to: Memory control blocks damaged.)\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003eThe name of the stealer (PurpleWave) and the version (1.0) are hardcoded and encrypted in the binary. Most of the strings in the binary are encrypted, but they getВ decrypted on runtime with the help of the decryption loop present in the binary (shown in Figure 6).\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cimg alt=\"Common Decryption function for encrypted strings in binary\" data-entity-type=\"\" data-entity-uuid=\"\" src=\"https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/purple_decryptionloop.PNG\" loading=\"lazy\" decoding=\"async\"\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cem\u003eFigure 6: The common decryption function for the encrypted strings in the binary.\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003eThe PurpleWave binary creates a mutex with the name вҖңMutexCantRepeatThisвҖқ to avoid multiple executions of malware instances. After that, it sends the HTTP POST request with the custom header and body to the C\u0026amp;C URL to get the configuration data.\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cimg alt=\"Sending request to get the config data\" data-entity-type=\"\" data-entity-uuid=\"\" src=\"https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/purple_configolly.PNG\" loading=\"lazy\" decoding=\"async\"\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cem\u003eFigure 7:В Sending request to the C\u0026amp;C server to get the config data.\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003eIt creates an HTTP request header with content type as вҖңform-dataвҖқ. The boundary is assigned with вҖңboundaryaswellвҖқ to act as a marker and user agent is set with вҖңappвҖқ. It creates a request body with a form name as вҖңidвҖқ and the value assigned to it is 1.\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cimg alt=\"Request with custom header and body to get the configuration\" data-entity-type=\"\" data-entity-uuid=\"\" src=\"https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/wireshark_config.JPG\" loading=\"lazy\" decoding=\"async\"\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cem\u003eFigure 8: The configuration request with the custom header and body.\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003eThe received data contains the customized configuration, which may change per the binary. We have observed three different configurations and different hosts of the PurpleWave binaries.\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cimg alt=\"Configuration from different PurpleWave binaries\" data-entity-type=\"\" data-entity-uuid=\"\" src=\"https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/config_comapre.png\" loading=\"lazy\" decoding=\"async\"\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cem\u003eFigure 9: The configuration from different PurpleWave binaries.\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003edirs - It consists of directory information from which files to be collected.\u003cbr\u003e\r\nfake - It has the fake alert message to be shown to the user on execution.\u003cbr\u003e\r\nloaders - It consists of an additional module name to be installed on the infected system.\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003eFor Config-2, PurpleWave will traverse path вҖң%userprofile%/DesktopвҖқ and collect the files having extensions txt, doc and docx. In Config-3, it will not collect any files but it has a module named вҖңKv2TDW4OвҖқ in the loaders, which will get downloaded and executed on the system.\u003cbr\u003e\r\nВ \u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eInstalling additional modules\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003eFor installing additional modules mentioned in the received configuration (Config-3), PurpleWaveВ again creates an HTTP POST request with the same headers mentioned in the previous request to the C\u0026amp;C host followed by вҖң/loader/module_nameвҖқ.\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cimg alt=\"Request to download additional module\" data-entity-type=\"\" data-entity-uuid=\"\" decoding=\"async\"\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cem\u003eFigure 10: The request to download an additional module.\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003ePurpleWave enumerates the loaders list from a JSON configuration, downloads the module name from the C\u0026amp;C server and stores it in %appdata% directory, then executes it.\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cimg alt=\"Downloading and executing additional modules\" data-entity-type=\"\" data-entity-uuid=\"\" of stealing credentials, autofills data, card data, cookies, and browser history from Chromium and Mozilla.\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003eFor Chromium browsers, it fetches the login credentials the form of a form-data field with the names shown below followed by their value.\u003cbr\u003e\r\nUsername - browser[BrowserName][passwords][index][login]\u003cbr\u003e\r\nPassword - decoding=\"async\"\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cem\u003eFigure 15: A captured screenshot.\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003eAfter that, it collects all the information about infected systems, such as operating system, CPU info, GPU info, machine GUID, username, machine name, and more.\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cimg alt=\"Collected system info\" data-entity-type=\"\" data-entity-uuid=\"\" src=\"https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/about_send.png\" loading=\"lazy\" decoding=\"async\"\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cem\u003eFigure 16: TheВ system information collected by PurpleWave.\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003eThe stealer also collects the SSFN files from the Steam application. The Steam application is used for playing, discussing, and creating games. The SSFN file exists to verify the users each time they login to their Steam account. It fetches the Steam path from the registry вҖңSoftware\\\\Valve\\\\SteamвҖқ and reads all the SSFN files stored into the config directory.\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\r\nPurpleWave also steals session-related files from the Telegram application. It reads the value of the default key in the system registry branch вҖңHKCU\\Software\\Classes\\tdesktop.tg\\DefaultIconвҖқВ to obtain a path of Telegram and collects all the files starts with вҖңmapвҖқ in the вҖңD877F783D5D3EF8CвҖқ directory.\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\r\n\u003cimg alt=\"Collecting Steam data and Telegram data\" data-entity-type=\"\" data-entity-uuid=\"\" src=\"https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/steam_telegram.png\" loading=\"lazy\" decoding=\"async\"\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cem\u003eFigure 17:В Collecting Steam and Telegram data.\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003ePurpleWave merges all the collectedВ fileВ data, browser data, screenshots, Steam data, Telegram data, and system info, then sends it to a C\u0026amp;C server using an HTTP POST request.\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cimg alt=\"Sending stolen data to C\u0026amp;C server\" data-entity-type=\"\" data-entity-uuid=\"\" src=\"https://cms.zscaler.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto/sites/default/files/images/blogs/sadique/purplewave/gate_post.JPG\" loading=\"lazy\" decoding=\"async\"\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cem\u003eFigure 18:В Sending stolen data to C\u0026amp;C server\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003eВ \u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eCoverage\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003eThe observed indicators in this attack were successfully blocked by the Zscaler Cloud Sandbox.\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cimg alt=\"The Zscaler Cloud Sandbox report for the PurpleWave Stealer\" sandbox detections, ZscalerвҖҷs multilayered cloud security platform detects indicators at various levels. The following advanced threat protection signatures have been released for detecting the malware:\u003cbr\u003e\r\n\u003ca href=\"https://threatlibrary.zscaler.com/?keyword=Win32.PWS.PurpleWave\"\u003eWin32.PWS.PurpleWave\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eConclusion\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003eZscaler believes that PurpleWave represents an active and ongoing threat, as theВ C\u0026amp;CВ servers are still alive and responding as of this writing.В The malware also still appears to be available for purchase on the black market. PurpleWave has incredible potential to steal sensitive information. The malware is in the early stages of development, with the author likely to enhance its stealing capabilities and add more features. We will continue to keep track of this threatВ to ensure coverage.\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://attack.mitre.org/\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e\u003cu\u003eMITRE
